2021: Just before the bike procession passed, one of the spectators with one foot crossed into the road and abruptly shoved a sign saying 'Cheer up, Grandpa and Grandma (allez opi omi)' towards the broadcast camera.  As a result, Tony Martin, who was running along the edge of the road, hit a sign directly, and about 100 cars crashed and fell in a domino fashion, and some players gave up on the race due to an injury. He was even caught on camera during the match.  The person holding the sign that caused the accident fled the scene, and the tournament is planning to sue this person.  The spectator was eventually arrested in Rendezvous, France, three days after the incident.  The audience is a woman in her thirties of French nationality, she says she did this because she wanted to leave a message of cheering for her grandparents, who are just German, irrespective of the match.  The Tour de France side said that it would not file a lawsuit as the spectators repented and appealed for leniency, but the French prosecutor's office is still in the process of reviewing whether or not to indict.  French prosecutors say that they plan to prosecute regardless of the will of the Tour de France, and that there is a possibility that the players' teams and individual players may file a lawsuit against the spectators.  A fine of 1,200 euros (about 1,600,000 won) was imposed.

sign with the words *â€œALLEZ OPI-OMI,â€* a mixture of French and German that translates to *â€œCome on grandpa-grandma!â€ or  "Go grandpa-grandma."* From sportingnews.com  What does 'allez opi-omi' mean?  The sign is a combination of two languages, French and German. "Allez" means "go" in French, according to Google Translate, while "opi" and "omi" are German terms for "grandpa" and "grandma," according to Dict.cc. So the sign would translate to "Go grandpa-grandma."
